## cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md
cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md:26 - mem0 CLI is the official command-line interface for [mem0](https://mem0.ai) -- the memory layer for AI agents. It lets developers and AI agents add, search, list, update, and delete memories via the mem0 Platform API from the terminal.
cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md:160 - - Interactive mode: prints banner, prompts for API key (masked with `*`), prompts for default user ID (default: `mem0-cli`), validates connection, saves config.
cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md:173 - Add a memory from text, messages, file, or stdin.
cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md:312 - mem0 get abc-123-def-456
cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md:313 - mem0 get abc-123-def-456 -o json
cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md:447 - 1. **Single memory:** `mem0 delete <memory_id>` -- deletes one memory by ID. Cannot combine with `--all` or `--entity`.
cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md:448 - 2. **Bulk delete:** `mem0 delete --all [scope]` -- deletes all memories matching scope filters. Use `--project` with `--all` to wipe all memories project-wide (sends wildcard `*` entity IDs). Cannot combine with `<memory_id>` or `--entity`.
cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md:449 - 3. **Entity cascade:** `mem0 delete --entity [scope]` -- deletes the entity itself and all its memories. Cannot combine with `<memory_id>` or `--all`.
cli\CLI_SPECIFICATION.md:454 - - Single: fetches the memory via `GET`, displays it, then prints "No changes made."

## openclaw\README.md
openclaw\README.md:3 - Long-term memory for [OpenClaw](https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw) agents, powered by [Mem0](https://mem0.ai).
openclaw\README.md:34 - - **User (long-term)** — The agent can explicitly store long-term memories using the `memory_store` tool (with `longTerm: true`, the default). These persist across all sessions for the user.
openclaw\README.md:38 - The agent tools (`memory_search`, `memory_list`) accept a `scope` parameter (`"session"`, `"long-term"`, or `"all"`) to control which memories are queried. The `memory_store` tool accepts a `longTerm` boolean (default: `true`) to choose where to store.
openclaw\README.md:44 - In multi-agent setups, each agent automatically gets its own memory namespace. Session keys following the pattern `agent:<agentId>:<uuid>` are parsed to derive isolated namespaces (`${userId}:agent:${agentId}`). Single-agent deployments are unaffected — plain session keys and `agent:main:*` keys resolve to the configured `userId`.
openclaw\README.md:61 - All memory tools (`memory_search`, `memory_store`, `memory_list`, `memory_forget`) accept an optional `agentId` parameter to query another agent's namespace:
openclaw\README.md:64 - memory_search({ query: "user's tech stack", agentId: "researcher" })
openclaw\README.md:77 - The plugin automatically skips recall and capture for non-interactive triggers: `cron`, `heartbeat`, `automation`, and `schedule`. Detection works via both `ctx.trigger` and session key patterns (`:cron:`, `:heartbeat:`). This prevents system-generated noise from polluting long-term memory.
openclaw\README.md:101 - Get an API key from [app.mem0.ai](https://app.mem0.ai), then add to your `openclaw.json`:
openclaw\README.md:220 - > **SQLite resilience:** If the history DB fails to initialize (e.g. native binding resolution under jiti), the plugin automatically retries with history disabled. Core memory operations (add, search, get, delete) work without the history DB.
